msg:I chose Sheraton when I went to Tanglang this time, and it did not disappoint. The room is clean and the facilities are relatively new. The 5th floor is the fitness center. It takes a while to get to the 5th floor by elevator. The swimming pool and gym are OK. I didn't bring swimming trunks, so I bought one inside. The service was good. The lifeguard in the swimming pool did not greet me, and training should be strengthened. After entering, the lifeguard said: You need to take a shower before going into the water! I told her we were going out for fun, and she asked me to come back later and pick up the room card at the front desk. At that time, I asked her if I could just come directly to the front desk to pick up the card? She said yes! In the end I had to do what she said. When we came back in the evening, we were all tired, so I quickly went to the front desk to get the card. The female clerk was still there at the time, so I went over and told her directly that I had only checked in to one room in the afternoon and now I wanted to get the room card for the other room. , she actually ignored and asked me to queue up! In the end, I queued up as she said. I also asked her if she had already queued up in the afternoon. You also said that you can just come over. Why do I have to queue up again now? She kept silent and ignored me, as if she couldn't hear me. Her way of dealing with it really made me feel very helpless! I also want to know how your hotel trains front desk staff? Is this the first time this kind of incident has happened since it opened? There are also the following points:
Point 1: I had already queued up when I checked in in the afternoon. Your hotel was unable to hand over the room to me when I checked in at 14:00 that afternoon, so why waste our time waiting in line to get the room? Where's the card?
Point 2: The female staff member asked me to come back in the evening and go directly to the front desk to get my room card. Why did I have to wait in line again until she had processed all the guests? Am I not a customer?
Point 3: The way the female staff handled things really opened our eyes. We also felt disrespected, which made our stay unpleasant.
Having stayed in dozens of mainland hotels and chain hotels, I deeply understand the importance of hotel staff training and how to make customers feel valued. Therefore, no comparison does no harm, and I hope your hotel can learn from it.
All in all, the design of the hotel room is not good. But service has always represented the image of a hotel, so it is important to make guests feel at home.
Thanks!
